{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-sonnet-4-6","id":"msg_01HayY1z6zhtBkSpEraviV61","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_0114HWtfdRxaxN7kDVQp9nAW","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# client-go Advanced Systems Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n`client-go` is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It lives in the Kubernetes monorepo under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/` and is periodically published to a standalone module. Its version tag `v0.X.Y` directly tracks Kubernetes release `v1.X.Y`.\n\n**What client-go is responsible for:**\n- Providing typed, dynamic, and metadata-only access to the Kubernetes API server over HTTP/HTTPS.\n- Managing authentication credential loading and injection (kubeconfig, in-cluster service accounts, exec plugins, OIDC).\n- Implementing the informer/cache machinery that powers every controller in the Kubernetes control plane.\n- Offering high-level utilities: work queues, leader election, server-side apply builders, and event recording.\n\n**What it explicitly does not own:**\n- API type definitions live in `k8s.io/api` and `k8s.io/apimachinery`.\n- Code-generation tooling lives in `k8s.io/code-generator`.\n- The API server's watch cache, etcd, and any server-side logic.\n\n**Upstream dependencies** (consumed by client-go):\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery` — runtime, schema, serialization, and watch primitives.\n- `k8s.io/api` — concrete typed API objects (Pod, Deployment, etc.).\n- `golang.org/x/time/rate` — token-bucket rate limiter used in work queues.\n\n**Downstream consumers** (built on top of client-go):\n- Every Kubernetes built-in controller (`kube-controller-manager`).\n- The Kubernetes scheduler.\n- Third-party operators and controllers via `controller-runtime`.\n- `kubectl` (uses client-go's `rest`, `dynamic`, and `discovery` packages directly).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe library divides into four logical tiers.\n\n### Tier 1: Transport and Configuration\n\n**`rest/config.go` — `rest.Config`**\n\nThe in-memory representation of all connection parameters: API server host, TLS settings, authentication credentials, QPS/burst limits, and a custom `http.RoundTripper` chain. The defaults (`DefaultQPS = 5.0`, `DefaultBurst = 10`) are defined here and are deliberately conservative. Authentication fields include `BearerToken`, `BearerTokenFile` (periodically re-read), `ExecProvider` (exec-based credential plugins), and `AuthProvider` (legacy auth providers). The `WrapTransport` field accepts a `transport.WrapperFunc` that layers a custom `RoundTripper` on top of the base transport.\n\n**`transport/transport.go` — transport layer**\n\n`transport.New(config)` produces the final `http.RoundTripper`. It retrieves a base TLS transport from a process-wide `tlsCache` (to reuse TLS sessions and avoid redundant handshakes) and then wraps it with `HTTPWrappersForConfig`, injecting authentication and other per-request decorators as a middleware chain.\n\n**`tools/clientcmd/` — kubeconfig parsing**\n\nLoads, merges, and resolves `kubeconfig` files, converting the on-disk representation into a `rest.Config`. This package owns all kubeconfig precedence logic (`--kubeconfig` flag, `KUBECONFIG` env, `~/.kube/config`).\n\n### Tier 2: HTTP Request Layer\n\n**`rest/client.go` — `RESTClient`**\n\nThe lowest-level HTTP client. Built from a `rest.Config`, it exposes a builder pattern: `.Verb(\"GET\").Resource(\"pods\").Namespace(\"default\").Name(\"nginx\")`. It handles Kubernetes URL conventions and content negotiation (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR).\n\n**`rest/request.go` — `Request`**\n\nAssembles the final HTTP request. All path segments, query parameters, and headers are accumulated. Execution is deferred until a terminal method is called (`.Do(ctx)`, `.DoRaw(ctx)`, `.Stream(ctx)`, `.Watch(ctx)`). Rate limiting is enforced here via `flowcontrol.RateLimiter` before the HTTP call is issued. Throttle events exceeding `longThrottleLatency` (50ms) are logged; those exceeding `extraLongThrottleLatency` (1s) are logged at a higher verbosity.\n\n**`rest/with_retry.go` — retry logic**\n\nEncapsulates retry decisions. The `WithRetry` interface's `IsNextRetry` method handles 429 responses (reads `Retry-After` header) and 5xx responses. The default for mutating verbs is zero retries to avoid accidental double-writes; watch requests use up to 10 retries by default.\n\n### Tier 3: Client Models\n\n**`kubernetes/` — typed `Clientset`**\n\nGenerated code. Provides compile-time-safe access to all built-in GroupVersionResources. The entry point `kubernetes.NewForConfig(cfg)` returns a `Clientset` aggregating group-versioned clients (e.g., `clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(...)`). Each typed client delegates to an underlying `RESTClient`.\n\n**`dynamic/simple.go` — `DynamicClient`**\n\nRepresents every object as `unstructured.Unstructured`. Used by operators handling CRDs at runtime without generated code. Every call requires the caller to supply a `schema.GroupVersionResource`.\n\n**`discovery/` — `DiscoveryClient`**\n\nInterrogates `/api`, `/apis`, and `/openapi/v3` to determine which resources exist and their capabilities. The `CachedDiscoveryClient` writes this data to disk to avoid re-querying on every process start — important for controllers that call `restmapper.GetAPIGroupResources` during startup.\n\n**`metadata/` — `MetadataClient`**\n\nA specialized client that requests objects using the `Accept: application/json;as=PartialObjectMetadata` header, instructing the API server to return only `ObjectMeta`. Used by garbage collection and other controllers that do not need full object bodies, significantly reducing bandwidth and memory cost.\n\n### Tier 4: Controller Infrastructure\n\n**`tools/cache/` — informer machinery**\n\nThe core of the controller model. A `SharedIndexInformer` maintains an eventually-consistent local cache of a given resource type. See Section 3 for the full data flow.\n\n**`util/workqueue/` — work queues**\n\nProvides `TypedInterface[T]`, `TypedDelayingInterface[T]`, and `TypedRateLimitingInterface[T]` — a layered set of queues used to decouple event detection from reconciliation.\n\n**`tools/leaderelection/` — leader election**\n\nEnables high-availability controllers by having replicas compete to acquire a `Lease` object on the API server. Only the current leader runs `OnStartedLeading`.\n\n**`applyconfigurations/` — server-side apply builders**\n\nGenerated type-safe structs that express desired state as partial objects, used with the `Apply` verb for safe multi-owner mutation.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3a. Single API Request\n\n1. **Client code** calls `clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"nginx\", metav1.GetOptions{})`.\n2. The generated typed client calls `r.c.Get()` on the underlying `RESTClient`.\n3. `RESTClient` constructs a `Request` (`rest/request.go`). The path is assembled as `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/nginx`.\n4. **Rate limiting**: `Request.tryThrottle()` calls `rateLimiter.Accept()`, blocking if the client is above its configured QPS.\n5. **HTTP execution**: `http.Client.Do()` is invoked. The transport chain runs: TLS session reuse → auth token injection → user-agent injection.\n6. The response body is deserialized by the runtime codec into a typed `*v1.Pod`. Non-2xx responses are deserialized into `*errors.StatusError`, enabling checks like `errors.IsNotFound(err)`.\n\n### 3b. Informer Startup and the Controller Loop\n\nThis is the canonical controller pattern. The data flow, from `ARCHITECTURE.md` and implemented across `tools/cache/`, is:\n\n```\nAPI Server\n    │\n    │  LIST (paginated) then WATCH\n    ▼\nReflector              tools/cache/reflector.go\n    │\n    │  store.Add / Update / Delete / Replace\n    ▼\nDeltaFIFO              tools/cache/delta_fifo.go\n    │\n    │  Pop() → HandleDeltas()\n    ▼\nsharedIndexInformer    tools/cache/shared_informer.go\n    ├── Updates Indexer (ThreadSafeStore)\n    └── Notifies sharedProcessor → per-handler goroutines\n                                        │\n                                        │  queue.Add(key)\n                                        ▼\n                             TypedRateLimitingInterface\n                                        │\n                                        │  queue.Get() → reconcile()\n                                        ▼\n                             Controller business logic\n                                        │\n                                        │  lister.Get(key)  [in-memory]\n                                        ▼\n                                     Indexer\n```\n\n**Step 1 — Reflector initialization** (`reflector.go:RunWithContext`)\n\n`wait.BackoffUntil` drives a loop calling `r.ListAndWatchWithContext(ctx)`. On each iteration:\n- If the `WatchListClient` feature gate is enabled (beta, on by default since 1.35), the reflector attempts `r.watchList(ctx)` — a streaming WATCH with `sendInitialEvents=true` that delivers the full initial state via watch events rather than a bulk LIST. This is more memory-efficient on the API server.\n- Otherwise (or on fallback), `r.list(ctx)` is called. This uses `tools/pager` to issue paginated LIST requests, accumulating pages until the `continue` token is empty.\n- After the initial list, `r.watchWithResync(ctx, w)` enters the watch loop.\n\nThe backoff manager uses an 800ms base, 30s max, and 2-minute reset (`reflector.go:NewReflectorWithOptions`), designed to reduce API server load to ~0.22 QPS during an outage.\n\n**Step 2 — DeltaFIFO as a change buffer** (`delta_fifo.go`)\n\n`DeltaFIFO` is a producer-consumer queue that accumulates `Deltas` (a typed slice of changes) per object key. Multiple rapid changes to the same object are accumulated: rather than receiving a single MODIFIED event, the controller sees every intermediate state in order. The `Replace()` call (triggered by a completed LIST) synthesizes `Replaced` or `Sync` deltas for objects that were previously known but absent from the new list, producing implicit deletion notifications. Internally, `items map[string]Deltas` holds the accumulated changes while `queue []string` maintains FIFO ordering without duplicates.\n\n**Step 3 — sharedIndexInformer as multiplexer** (`shared_informer.go:sharedIndexInformer`)\n\n`RunWithContext` wires `DeltaFIFO`, `ListerWatcher`, and the `HandleDeltas` process function into an internal `Config` and starts a `controller`. In parallel goroutines, the `sharedProcessor` fans notifications to each registered `ResourceEventHandler`. The critical design: multiple independent controllers register handlers on the same informer, sharing a single LIST/WATCH connection. The `SharedInformerFactory` (`informers/factory.go:sharedInformerFactory`) deduplicates informers by Go type so that, e.g., two controllers watching Pods both share one informer.\n\n**Step 4 — Handler to work queue boundary**\n\nA well-written event handler calls only `queue.Add(key)`. The work queue deduplicates: if an object is enqueued multiple times before processing, only one entry exists. The controller calls `queue.Get()` to obtain the key, reconciles, and then must call `queue.Done(key)`. If reconciliation fails, it calls `queue.AddRateLimited(key)` to re-enqueue with backoff, and `queue.Forget(key)` on success to reset the per-item failure counter.\n\n**Step 5 — Controller reads from cache via Lister**\n\nInside the reconcile function, the controller fetches the object from the cache using a generated Lister (e.g., `podLister.Pods(\"default\").Get(\"nginx\")`). This is a pure in-memory read against the `Indexer`'s `ThreadSafeStore` — no API call is made. Only when a guaranteed-fresh view is strictly required should the controller bypass the cache and call the API directly.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Watch Expiry and Relist\n\nIf the API server's watch cache has advanced past the client's `resourceVersion`, the server returns `410 Gone`. The reflector treats this as non-fatal, sets `isLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable = true`, and re-lists from scratch. Watch bookmarks — empty `BOOKMARK` events the server sends periodically — advance the client's `lastSyncResourceVersion` without requiring a full relist, shrinking the recovery window after reconnect.\n\nThe per-watch timeout is randomized between `minWatchTimeout` and `2*minWatchTimeout` (default: a value between 5 and 10 minutes) to spread reconnection load across API server instances during rolling restarts.\n\n### Informer Sync vs. Cache Freshness\n\n`SharedInformer.HasSynced()` returns true only after the initial LIST has been processed and all pre-sync notifications have been delivered to all registered handlers. Calling `WaitForCacheSync` (`shared_informer.go`) before starting reconciliation is mandatory to avoid acting on a partial cache view. However, `HasSynced() == true` does not mean the cache reflects the present moment — only that it saw at least one complete snapshot. Stale reads are the fundamental trade-off of the cached model.\n\n### Work Queue Rate Limiting and Forget\n\n`DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter` (`util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`) combines two limiters via `MaxOfRateLimiter`:\n- `TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter`: per-item exponential backoff, starting at 5ms, capped at 1000s.\n- `TypedBucketRateLimiter`: global token-bucket at 10 QPS with a burst of 100.\n\nA controller that never calls `queue.Forget(key)` on success will accumulate exponential backoff state for that key indefinitely, eventually reducing reconciliation for that item to once every ~16 minutes.\n\n### Client-Side vs. Server-Side Rate Limiting\n\n`rest.Config.QPS` and `Burst` enforce a voluntary client-side token bucket. The server's API Priority and Fairness (APF) system enforces server-side limits independently. When the server returns 429, the `withRetry` logic reads `Retry-After` and waits. The two systems are complementary but not coordinated: a misconfigured client with very high QPS will exhaust its APF flow-schema quota and receive sustained 429s even if it respects its local token bucket.\n\n### Resync: In-Memory Re-Notification, Not API Round-Trips\n\nThe `ResyncPeriod` on an informer triggers periodic `Sync` deltas that re-deliver every object in the cache to all handlers. This does **not** contact the API server — it is purely in-memory. The purpose is to let controllers recover from silent reconciliation failures. The cost is proportional to the size of the cache: at 10,000 objects re-delivered every 10 minutes, a slow handler becomes a bottleneck. Setting resync too short inflates CPU; setting it to zero means the controller only heals on real watch events.\n\n### ThreadSafeStore and Mutation Risk\n\nThe `ThreadSafeStore` (`tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`) stores object pointers. Its thread-safety guarantees apply only if callers treat returned objects as read-only. Modifying a pointer returned by `Get` or `List` without copying it corrupts the index and is not detected at runtime in production builds. The `MutationDetector` (`tools/cache/mutation_detector.go`) catches this in test environments by deep-copying objects and comparing checksums periodically; it panics on detection.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### WrapTransport (`rest.Config.WrapTransport`)\n\nInjects a custom `http.RoundTripper` middleware. Used to add request signing, audit logging, or metrics collection. Risk: a wrapper that does not call the inner transport silently breaks all API calls. The config also accepts a `Transport` field for full replacement of the base transport, but this is incompatible with `TLSClientConfig`.\n\n### TransformFunc (`SharedInformer.SetTransform`)\n\nCalled for each object before it enters the cache. The function signature is `func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)`. It can return a structurally different object (e.g., a pruned copy). Must be set before `Run()` via `informer.SetTransform(fn)` or `factory.WithTransform(fn)` (`informers/factory.go:WithTransform`). Risk: modifying the incoming object in-place corrupts the reflector's internal state. Always work on a deep copy.\n\n### WatchErrorHandler (`SharedInformer.SetWatchErrorHandlerWithContext`)\n\nReplaces the default watch error logger. Must be set before `Run()`; attempting to set it after the informer starts returns an error. Must return quickly — the handler is called synchronously in the reflector loop, and a blocking handler delays reconnect.\n\n### Custom Indexers (`SharedIndexInformer.AddIndexers`)\n\nMust be called before `Run()`. An `IndexFunc` (`tools/cache/index.go:IndexFunc`) maps an object to one or more string index keys, enabling `ByIndex(indexName, value)` lookups in O(1) amortized time instead of full list scans. Risk: attempting to add indexers after `Run()` returns an error. Indexers that produce many values per object (e.g., one entry per label) can significantly increase the `storeIndex` memory footprint.\n\n### ResourceEventHandler Registration (`AddEventHandler` / `AddEventHandlerWithOptions`)\n\nReturns a `ResourceEventHandlerRegistration` whose `HasSynced()` is more fine-grained than the informer-level `HasSynced()` — it reports whether *this specific handler* has received all pre-sync notifications. This is the correct signal to gate reconciliation when handlers are added dynamically after informer startup.\n\n### Feature Gates (`features/known_features.go`)\n\nClient-side feature gates are controlled by environment variables (`KUBE_FEATURE_<Name>=true|false`). Gates of note:\n- `WatchListClient` (beta, default true at 1.35+): streaming initial state via WATCH rather than paginated LIST. Requires server support; falls back automatically.\n- `InOrderInformers` (beta, default true at 1.33+): ensures watch events are delivered to handlers in resource version order.\n- `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` (beta, default true at 1.35+): processes batches of delta events atomically for higher throughput; requires `Config.ProcessBatch` to be non-nil (`tools/cache/controller.go:Config`).\n- `AtomicFIFO` (beta, default true at 1.36+): enables atomic processing of all events for a single item popped from the FIFO.\n- `ClientsAllowCBOR` / `ClientsPreferCBOR` (alpha): opt-in to CBOR wire encoding, which is more compact than JSON for many object types.\n\n### Leader Election Callbacks (`tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`)\n\n`LeaderElectionConfig.Callbacks` requires `OnStartedLeading` and `OnStoppedLeading`. The conventional pattern is to call `os.Exit(1)` in `OnStoppedLeading` to force a clean process restart rather than continuing in an ambiguous state. The timing invariant `LeaseDuration > RenewDeadline > RetryPeriod * JitterFactor` is enforced by `NewLeaderElector`; violating it returns an error. Clock skew tolerance is configurable by adjusting the ratio of `LeaseDuration` to `RenewDeadline`.\n\n### Server-Side Apply (`applyconfigurations/`)\n\n`applyconfigurations` provides generated type-safe builders for SSA patch objects. The `utils.go` helpers (e.g., `ExtractPod`) extract an existing object's apply configuration from a live object — the correct starting point for computing a desired-state patch that preserves field ownership. Using raw JSON merge-patch for SSA is an anti-pattern that loses ownership information and can cause unintended field clearing.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### Informer Cache Memory\n\nEach `sharedIndexInformer` holds a full decoded copy of every watched object. In large clusters (thousands of Pods, ConfigMaps, or Secrets), the aggregate cache across all informers in a controller process can reach gigabytes. Mitigation strategies:\n\n1. **`TransformFunc`**: strip `ManagedFields`, large annotations, and unused status fields before objects enter the cache. Set via `informers/factory.go:WithTransform` or `SharedInformer.SetTransform` before `Run()`.\n2. **`WithNamespace`** (`informers/factory.go`): limits the factory to one namespace, filtering at the API server.\n3. **`WithTweakListOptions`** (`informers/factory.go`): injects label or field selectors into the ListerWatcher, narrowing the watched set without changing the informer interface.\n4. **`MetadataClient`** (`metadata/`): for controllers that only need `ObjectMeta`, requesting `PartialObjectMetadata` eliminates spec/status decoding entirely.\n\n### TLS Connection Reuse and Pool Fragmentation\n\nThe `tlsCache` in `transport/transport.go` is a process-wide map keyed on transport configuration. Multiple `Clientset` instances created from equivalent `rest.Config` values share the same underlying `http.Transport` and connection pool. Creating many `rest.Config` objects with subtly different values (e.g., different `UserAgent` strings) bypasses the cache and fragments the connection pool, causing TCP connection proliferation at the API server.\n\n### Reconnect Jitter and Thundering Herds\n\nEach reflector randomizes its watch timeout between `minWatchTimeout` and `2*minWatchTimeout`. This prevents all controllers across a fleet from reconnecting simultaneously after an API server restart, which would otherwise produce a burst of LIST requests that can saturate etcd and the API server's watch cache simultaneously.\n\n### Resync Period Selection\n\nA resync period of 10–30 minutes is typical. Too short: CPU spikes as thousands of objects are re-delivered per cycle. Too long (or zero): the controller relies entirely on real watch events and cannot self-heal from missed events or logic bugs that left objects in a bad state without generating a new event. Zero resync is appropriate only for controllers with well-understood reconciliation semantics.\n\n### Controller Throughput with Batch Processing\n\nWith `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` enabled (default at 1.35+), the internal `controller` invokes `Config.ProcessBatch` (`tools/cache/controller.go`) with a slice of `Delta` objects rather than calling `Config.Process` once per delta. This reduces per-delta overhead and increases throughput for bursty updates. The `TransactionError` type from `tools/cache/store.go` is used to signal partial batch failures, allowing the informer to re-enqueue only the unprocessed items.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n`client-go` is the official Go client library for the Kubernetes API. It lives in the Kubernetes monorepo under `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/` and is periodically published to a standalone module. Its version tag `v0.X.Y` directly tracks Kubernetes release `v1.X.Y`.\n\n**What client-go is responsible for:**\n- Providing typed, dynamic, and metadata-only access to the Kubernetes API server over HTTP/HTTPS.\n- Managing authentication credential loading and injection (kubeconfig, in-cluster service accounts, exec plugins, OIDC).\n- Implementing the informer/cache machinery that powers every controller in the Kubernetes control plane.\n- Offering high-level utilities: work queues, leader election, server-side apply builders, and event recording.\n\n**What it explicitly does not own:**\n- API type definitions live in `k8s.io/api` and `k8s.io/apimachinery`.\n- Code-generation tooling lives in `k8s.io/code-generator`.\n- The API server's watch cache, etcd, and any server-side logic.\n\n**Upstream dependencies** (consumed by client-go):\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery` — runtime, schema, serialization, and watch primitives.\n- `k8s.io/api` — concrete typed API objects (Pod, Deployment, etc.).\n- `golang.org/x/time/rate` — token-bucket rate limiter used in work queues.\n\n**Downstream consumers** (built on top of client-go):\n- Every Kubernetes built-in controller (`kube-controller-manager`).\n- The Kubernetes scheduler.\n- Third-party operators and controllers via `controller-runtime`.\n- `kubectl` (uses client-go's `rest`, `dynamic`, and `discovery` packages directly).\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\nThe library divides into four logical tiers.\n\n### Tier 1: Transport and Configuration\n\n**`rest/config.go` — `rest.Config`**\n\nThe in-memory representation of all connection parameters: API server host, TLS settings, authentication credentials, QPS/burst limits, and a custom `http.RoundTripper` chain. The defaults (`DefaultQPS = 5.0`, `DefaultBurst = 10`) are defined here and are deliberately conservative. Authentication fields include `BearerToken`, `BearerTokenFile` (periodically re-read), `ExecProvider` (exec-based credential plugins), and `AuthProvider` (legacy auth providers). The `WrapTransport` field accepts a `transport.WrapperFunc` that layers a custom `RoundTripper` on top of the base transport.\n\n**`transport/transport.go` — transport layer**\n\n`transport.New(config)` produces the final `http.RoundTripper`. It retrieves a base TLS transport from a process-wide `tlsCache` (to reuse TLS sessions and avoid redundant handshakes) and then wraps it with `HTTPWrappersForConfig`, injecting authentication and other per-request decorators as a middleware chain.\n\n**`tools/clientcmd/` — kubeconfig parsing**\n\nLoads, merges, and resolves `kubeconfig` files, converting the on-disk representation into a `rest.Config`. This package owns all kubeconfig precedence logic (`--kubeconfig` flag, `KUBECONFIG` env, `~/.kube/config`).\n\n### Tier 2: HTTP Request Layer\n\n**`rest/client.go` — `RESTClient`**\n\nThe lowest-level HTTP client. Built from a `rest.Config`, it exposes a builder pattern: `.Verb(\"GET\").Resource(\"pods\").Namespace(\"default\").Name(\"nginx\")`. It handles Kubernetes URL conventions and content negotiation (JSON, Protobuf, CBOR).\n\n**`rest/request.go` — `Request`**\n\nAssembles the final HTTP request. All path segments, query parameters, and headers are accumulated. Execution is deferred until a terminal method is called (`.Do(ctx)`, `.DoRaw(ctx)`, `.Stream(ctx)`, `.Watch(ctx)`). Rate limiting is enforced here via `flowcontrol.RateLimiter` before the HTTP call is issued. Throttle events exceeding `longThrottleLatency` (50ms) are logged; those exceeding `extraLongThrottleLatency` (1s) are logged at a higher verbosity.\n\n**`rest/with_retry.go` — retry logic**\n\nEncapsulates retry decisions. The `WithRetry` interface's `IsNextRetry` method handles 429 responses (reads `Retry-After` header) and 5xx responses. The default for mutating verbs is zero retries to avoid accidental double-writes; watch requests use up to 10 retries by default.\n\n### Tier 3: Client Models\n\n**`kubernetes/` — typed `Clientset`**\n\nGenerated code. Provides compile-time-safe access to all built-in GroupVersionResources. The entry point `kubernetes.NewForConfig(cfg)` returns a `Clientset` aggregating group-versioned clients (e.g., `clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(...)`). Each typed client delegates to an underlying `RESTClient`.\n\n**`dynamic/simple.go` — `DynamicClient`**\n\nRepresents every object as `unstructured.Unstructured`. Used by operators handling CRDs at runtime without generated code. Every call requires the caller to supply a `schema.GroupVersionResource`.\n\n**`discovery/` — `DiscoveryClient`**\n\nInterrogates `/api`, `/apis`, and `/openapi/v3` to determine which resources exist and their capabilities. The `CachedDiscoveryClient` writes this data to disk to avoid re-querying on every process start — important for controllers that call `restmapper.GetAPIGroupResources` during startup.\n\n**`metadata/` — `MetadataClient`**\n\nA specialized client that requests objects using the `Accept: application/json;as=PartialObjectMetadata` header, instructing the API server to return only `ObjectMeta`. Used by garbage collection and other controllers that do not need full object bodies, significantly reducing bandwidth and memory cost.\n\n### Tier 4: Controller Infrastructure\n\n**`tools/cache/` — informer machinery**\n\nThe core of the controller model. A `SharedIndexInformer` maintains an eventually-consistent local cache of a given resource type. See Section 3 for the full data flow.\n\n**`util/workqueue/` — work queues**\n\nProvides `TypedInterface[T]`, `TypedDelayingInterface[T]`, and `TypedRateLimitingInterface[T]` — a layered set of queues used to decouple event detection from reconciliation.\n\n**`tools/leaderelection/` — leader election**\n\nEnables high-availability controllers by having replicas compete to acquire a `Lease` object on the API server. Only the current leader runs `OnStartedLeading`.\n\n**`applyconfigurations/` — server-side apply builders**\n\nGenerated type-safe structs that express desired state as partial objects, used with the `Apply` verb for safe multi-owner mutation.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3a. Single API Request\n\n1. **Client code** calls `clientset.CoreV1().Pods(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"nginx\", metav1.GetOptions{})`.\n2. The generated typed client calls `r.c.Get()` on the underlying `RESTClient`.\n3. `RESTClient` constructs a `Request` (`rest/request.go`). The path is assembled as `/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/nginx`.\n4. **Rate limiting**: `Request.tryThrottle()` calls `rateLimiter.Accept()`, blocking if the client is above its configured QPS.\n5. **HTTP execution**: `http.Client.Do()` is invoked. The transport chain runs: TLS session reuse → auth token injection → user-agent injection.\n6. The response body is deserialized by the runtime codec into a typed `*v1.Pod`. Non-2xx responses are deserialized into `*errors.StatusError`, enabling checks like `errors.IsNotFound(err)`.\n\n### 3b. Informer Startup and the Controller Loop\n\nThis is the canonical controller pattern. The data flow, from `ARCHITECTURE.md` and implemented across `tools/cache/`, is:\n\n```\nAPI Server\n    │\n    │  LIST (paginated) then WATCH\n    ▼\nReflector              tools/cache/reflector.go\n    │\n    │  store.Add / Update / Delete / Replace\n    ▼\nDeltaFIFO              tools/cache/delta_fifo.go\n    │\n    │  Pop() → HandleDeltas()\n    ▼\nsharedIndexInformer    tools/cache/shared_informer.go\n    ├── Updates Indexer (ThreadSafeStore)\n    └── Notifies sharedProcessor → per-handler goroutines\n                                        │\n                                        │  queue.Add(key)\n                                        ▼\n                             TypedRateLimitingInterface\n                                        │\n                                        │  queue.Get() → reconcile()\n                                        ▼\n                             Controller business logic\n                                        │\n                                        │  lister.Get(key)  [in-memory]\n                                        ▼\n                                     Indexer\n```\n\n**Step 1 — Reflector initialization** (`reflector.go:RunWithContext`)\n\n`wait.BackoffUntil` drives a loop calling `r.ListAndWatchWithContext(ctx)`. On each iteration:\n- If the `WatchListClient` feature gate is enabled (beta, on by default since 1.35), the reflector attempts `r.watchList(ctx)` — a streaming WATCH with `sendInitialEvents=true` that delivers the full initial state via watch events rather than a bulk LIST. This is more memory-efficient on the API server.\n- Otherwise (or on fallback), `r.list(ctx)` is called. This uses `tools/pager` to issue paginated LIST requests, accumulating pages until the `continue` token is empty.\n- After the initial list, `r.watchWithResync(ctx, w)` enters the watch loop.\n\nThe backoff manager uses an 800ms base, 30s max, and 2-minute reset (`reflector.go:NewReflectorWithOptions`), designed to reduce API server load to ~0.22 QPS during an outage.\n\n**Step 2 — DeltaFIFO as a change buffer** (`delta_fifo.go`)\n\n`DeltaFIFO` is a producer-consumer queue that accumulates `Deltas` (a typed slice of changes) per object key. Multiple rapid changes to the same object are accumulated: rather than receiving a single MODIFIED event, the controller sees every intermediate state in order. The `Replace()` call (triggered by a completed LIST) synthesizes `Replaced` or `Sync` deltas for objects that were previously known but absent from the new list, producing implicit deletion notifications. Internally, `items map[string]Deltas` holds the accumulated changes while `queue []string` maintains FIFO ordering without duplicates.\n\n**Step 3 — sharedIndexInformer as multiplexer** (`shared_informer.go:sharedIndexInformer`)\n\n`RunWithContext` wires `DeltaFIFO`, `ListerWatcher`, and the `HandleDeltas` process function into an internal `Config` and starts a `controller`. In parallel goroutines, the `sharedProcessor` fans notifications to each registered `ResourceEventHandler`. The critical design: multiple independent controllers register handlers on the same informer, sharing a single LIST/WATCH connection. The `SharedInformerFactory` (`informers/factory.go:sharedInformerFactory`) deduplicates informers by Go type so that, e.g., two controllers watching Pods both share one informer.\n\n**Step 4 — Handler to work queue boundary**\n\nA well-written event handler calls only `queue.Add(key)`. The work queue deduplicates: if an object is enqueued multiple times before processing, only one entry exists. The controller calls `queue.Get()` to obtain the key, reconciles, and then must call `queue.Done(key)`. If reconciliation fails, it calls `queue.AddRateLimited(key)` to re-enqueue with backoff, and `queue.Forget(key)` on success to reset the per-item failure counter.\n\n**Step 5 — Controller reads from cache via Lister**\n\nInside the reconcile function, the controller fetches the object from the cache using a generated Lister (e.g., `podLister.Pods(\"default\").Get(\"nginx\")`). This is a pure in-memory read against the `Indexer`'s `ThreadSafeStore` — no API call is made. Only when a guaranteed-fresh view is strictly required should the controller bypass the cache and call the API directly.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Watch Expiry and Relist\n\nIf the API server's watch cache has advanced past the client's `resourceVersion`, the server returns `410 Gone`. The reflector treats this as non-fatal, sets `isLastSyncResourceVersionUnavailable = true`, and re-lists from scratch. Watch bookmarks — empty `BOOKMARK` events the server sends periodically — advance the client's `lastSyncResourceVersion` without requiring a full relist, shrinking the recovery window after reconnect.\n\nThe per-watch timeout is randomized between `minWatchTimeout` and `2*minWatchTimeout` (default: a value between 5 and 10 minutes) to spread reconnection load across API server instances during rolling restarts.\n\n### Informer Sync vs. Cache Freshness\n\n`SharedInformer.HasSynced()` returns true only after the initial LIST has been processed and all pre-sync notifications have been delivered to all registered handlers. Calling `WaitForCacheSync` (`shared_informer.go`) before starting reconciliation is mandatory to avoid acting on a partial cache view. However, `HasSynced() == true` does not mean the cache reflects the present moment — only that it saw at least one complete snapshot. Stale reads are the fundamental trade-off of the cached model.\n\n### Work Queue Rate Limiting and Forget\n\n`DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter` (`util/workqueue/default_rate_limiters.go`) combines two limiters via `MaxOfRateLimiter`:\n- `TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter`: per-item exponential backoff, starting at 5ms, capped at 1000s.\n- `TypedBucketRateLimiter`: global token-bucket at 10 QPS with a burst of 100.\n\nA controller that never calls `queue.Forget(key)` on success will accumulate exponential backoff state for that key indefinitely, eventually reducing reconciliation for that item to once every ~16 minutes.\n\n### Client-Side vs. Server-Side Rate Limiting\n\n`rest.Config.QPS` and `Burst` enforce a voluntary client-side token bucket. The server's API Priority and Fairness (APF) system enforces server-side limits independently. When the server returns 429, the `withRetry` logic reads `Retry-After` and waits. The two systems are complementary but not coordinated: a misconfigured client with very high QPS will exhaust its APF flow-schema quota and receive sustained 429s even if it respects its local token bucket.\n\n### Resync: In-Memory Re-Notification, Not API Round-Trips\n\nThe `ResyncPeriod` on an informer triggers periodic `Sync` deltas that re-deliver every object in the cache to all handlers. This does **not** contact the API server — it is purely in-memory. The purpose is to let controllers recover from silent reconciliation failures. The cost is proportional to the size of the cache: at 10,000 objects re-delivered every 10 minutes, a slow handler becomes a bottleneck. Setting resync too short inflates CPU; setting it to zero means the controller only heals on real watch events.\n\n### ThreadSafeStore and Mutation Risk\n\nThe `ThreadSafeStore` (`tools/cache/thread_safe_store.go`) stores object pointers. Its thread-safety guarantees apply only if callers treat returned objects as read-only. Modifying a pointer returned by `Get` or `List` without copying it corrupts the index and is not detected at runtime in production builds. The `MutationDetector` (`tools/cache/mutation_detector.go`) catches this in test environments by deep-copying objects and comparing checksums periodically; it panics on detection.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Risks\n\n### WrapTransport (`rest.Config.WrapTransport`)\n\nInjects a custom `http.RoundTripper` middleware. Used to add request signing, audit logging, or metrics collection. Risk: a wrapper that does not call the inner transport silently breaks all API calls. The config also accepts a `Transport` field for full replacement of the base transport, but this is incompatible with `TLSClientConfig`.\n\n### TransformFunc (`SharedInformer.SetTransform`)\n\nCalled for each object before it enters the cache. The function signature is `func(interface{}) (interface{}, error)`. It can return a structurally different object (e.g., a pruned copy). Must be set before `Run()` via `informer.SetTransform(fn)` or `factory.WithTransform(fn)` (`informers/factory.go:WithTransform`). Risk: modifying the incoming object in-place corrupts the reflector's internal state. Always work on a deep copy.\n\n### WatchErrorHandler (`SharedInformer.SetWatchErrorHandlerWithContext`)\n\nReplaces the default watch error logger. Must be set before `Run()`; attempting to set it after the informer starts returns an error. Must return quickly — the handler is called synchronously in the reflector loop, and a blocking handler delays reconnect.\n\n### Custom Indexers (`SharedIndexInformer.AddIndexers`)\n\nMust be called before `Run()`. An `IndexFunc` (`tools/cache/index.go:IndexFunc`) maps an object to one or more string index keys, enabling `ByIndex(indexName, value)` lookups in O(1) amortized time instead of full list scans. Risk: attempting to add indexers after `Run()` returns an error. Indexers that produce many values per object (e.g., one entry per label) can significantly increase the `storeIndex` memory footprint.\n\n### ResourceEventHandler Registration (`AddEventHandler` / `AddEventHandlerWithOptions`)\n\nReturns a `ResourceEventHandlerRegistration` whose `HasSynced()` is more fine-grained than the informer-level `HasSynced()` — it reports whether *this specific handler* has received all pre-sync notifications. This is the correct signal to gate reconciliation when handlers are added dynamically after informer startup.\n\n### Feature Gates (`features/known_features.go`)\n\nClient-side feature gates are controlled by environment variables (`KUBE_FEATURE_<Name>=true|false`). Gates of note:\n- `WatchListClient` (beta, default true at 1.35+): streaming initial state via WATCH rather than paginated LIST. Requires server support; falls back automatically.\n- `InOrderInformers` (beta, default true at 1.33+): ensures watch events are delivered to handlers in resource version order.\n- `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` (beta, default true at 1.35+): processes batches of delta events atomically for higher throughput; requires `Config.ProcessBatch` to be non-nil (`tools/cache/controller.go:Config`).\n- `AtomicFIFO` (beta, default true at 1.36+): enables atomic processing of all events for a single item popped from the FIFO.\n- `ClientsAllowCBOR` / `ClientsPreferCBOR` (alpha): opt-in to CBOR wire encoding, which is more compact than JSON for many object types.\n\n### Leader Election Callbacks (`tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`)\n\n`LeaderElectionConfig.Callbacks` requires `OnStartedLeading` and `OnStoppedLeading`. The conventional pattern is to call `os.Exit(1)` in `OnStoppedLeading` to force a clean process restart rather than continuing in an ambiguous state. The timing invariant `LeaseDuration > RenewDeadline > RetryPeriod * JitterFactor` is enforced by `NewLeaderElector`; violating it returns an error. Clock skew tolerance is configurable by adjusting the ratio of `LeaseDuration` to `RenewDeadline`.\n\n### Server-Side Apply (`applyconfigurations/`)\n\n`applyconfigurations` provides generated type-safe builders for SSA patch objects. The `utils.go` helpers (e.g., `ExtractPod`) extract an existing object's apply configuration from a live object — the correct starting point for computing a desired-state patch that preserves field ownership. Using raw JSON merge-patch for SSA is an anti-pattern that loses ownership information and can cause unintended field clearing.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications\n\n### Informer Cache Memory\n\nEach `sharedIndexInformer` holds a full decoded copy of every watched object. In large clusters (thousands of Pods, ConfigMaps, or Secrets), the aggregate cache across all informers in a controller process can reach gigabytes. Mitigation strategies:\n\n1. **`TransformFunc`**: strip `ManagedFields`, large annotations, and unused status fields before objects enter the cache. Set via `informers/factory.go:WithTransform` or `SharedInformer.SetTransform` before `Run()`.\n2. **`WithNamespace`** (`informers/factory.go`): limits the factory to one namespace, filtering at the API server.\n3. **`WithTweakListOptions`** (`informers/factory.go`): injects label or field selectors into the ListerWatcher, narrowing the watched set without changing the informer interface.\n4. **`MetadataClient`** (`metadata/`): for controllers that only need `ObjectMeta`, requesting `PartialObjectMetadata` eliminates spec/status decoding entirely.\n\n### TLS Connection Reuse and Pool Fragmentation\n\nThe `tlsCache` in `transport/transport.go` is a process-wide map keyed on transport configuration. Multiple `Clientset` instances created from equivalent `rest.Config` values share the same underlying `http.Transport` and connection pool. Creating many `rest.Config` objects with subtly different values (e.g., different `UserAgent` strings) bypasses the cache and fragments the connection pool, causing TCP connection proliferation at the API server.\n\n### Reconnect Jitter and Thundering Herds\n\nEach reflector randomizes its watch timeout between `minWatchTimeout` and `2*minWatchTimeout`. This prevents all controllers across a fleet from reconnecting simultaneously after an API server restart, which would otherwise produce a burst of LIST requests that can saturate etcd and the API server's watch cache simultaneously.\n\n### Resync Period Selection\n\nA resync period of 10–30 minutes is typical. Too short: CPU spikes as thousands of objects are re-delivered per cycle. Too long (or zero): the controller relies entirely on real watch events and cannot self-heal from missed events or logic bugs that left objects in a bad state without generating a new event. Zero resync is appropriate only for controllers with well-understood reconciliation semantics.\n\n### Controller Throughput with Batch Processing\n\nWith `InOrderInformersBatchProcess` enabled (default at 1.35+), the internal `controller` invokes `Config.ProcessBatch` (`tools/cache/controller.go`) with a slice of `Delta` objects rather than calling `Config.Process` once per delta. This reduces per-delta overhead and increases throughput for bursty updates. The `TransactionError` type from `tools/cache/store.go` is used to signal partial batch failures, allowing the informer to re-enqueue only the unprocessed items.\n\n---\n\n## 7.
